  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_07bbae55-a61a-4fc3-8408-4ade6a921d63'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/35287610-janet-ridge">Janet Ridge</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Oddly enough, I began the series with this very book (found in isolation on a library shelf), then looped back to fill in the background of Harry Dres<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Oddly enough, I began the series with this very book (found in isolation on a library shelf), then looped back to fill in the background of Harry Dresden's life. I can assure you that it's perfectly easy to follow along, and all the important connections are explained thoroughly without any boring expository drag. Here's the advantage to coming at the series this way: Butcher's writing gets MUCH better as it goes along, and the stories get more exciting as Dresden builds up power and allies. I am a huge fan, but I can still barely choke down Fool Moon. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">And if a stranger started reading any one of the series, wouldn't they be lost if it weren't for the brief exposition he gives?<br/>That repetition isn't f<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">And if a stranger started reading any one of the series, wouldn't they be lost if it weren't for the brief exposition he gives?<br />That repetition isn't for us fans, its for the soon-to-be fan that is just now finding any of the books. <br />Every book could potentially be someone's first book in the series. I started on Turn Coat, and I've still never read them in order. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_3091106782" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3091106782" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3091106782?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10360293-ghost-story">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3091106782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5220959220253252054"><i>I have a Booktube channel now! Subscribe here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCRjhqBJPxVH2aevPk_TLM3w?view_as=subscriber'>https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCRjh...</a></i><br/><br/><b><i>Ghost Story</i> feels like a volume to reboot the series before it enter a new story arc, or the next season, in the life of Harry Dresden. </b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “It was never too late to learn something. The past is unalterable in any event. The future is the only thing we can change. Learning the lessons of the past is the only way to shape the present and the future.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>It is not an easy task to write a follow-up to <i>Chang</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5220959220253252054" style="display:none"><i>I have a Booktube channel now! Subscribe here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCRjhqBJPxVH2aevPk_TLM3w?view_as=subscriber">https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCRjh...</a></i><br><br><b><i>Ghost Story</i> feels like a volume to reboot the series before it enter a new story arc, or the next season, in the life of Harry Dresden. </b><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “It was never too late to learn something. The past is unalterable in any event. The future is the only thing we can change. Learning the lessons of the past is the only way to shape the present and the future.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>It is not an easy task to write a follow-up to <i>Changes</i>, and I have a slightly pessimistic outlook on how Butcher will write a single installment for the series that’s as good—or better—as <i>Changes</i>. I’ve heard spectacular things about <i>Skin Game</i>, though, so I’ll be keeping my hopeful heart in check for that one. As for this book, I’ve heard a lot of discouraging things about <i>Ghost Story</i> from fans of the series, some even called it THE worst book of the series, and that terrified me because <i>Fool Moon</i>—the second book in the series—almost pushed me off from continuing with the series. I shudder at the thought of reading a book in the series that’s more inferior than that. But as it turns out, I found that <i>Ghost Story</i> was still pretty good.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I always considered myself a loner.<br><br>I mean, not like a poor-me, Byron-esque, I-should-have-brought-a-swimming-buddy loner. I mean the sort of person who doesn’t feel too upset about the prospect of a weekend spent seeing no one, and reading good books on the couch. It wasn’t like I was a people hater or anything. I enjoyed activities and the company of friends. But they were a side dish. I always thought I would be happy without them.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I do think it’s understandable, though, why some readers found <i>Ghost Story</i>, the thirteenth book in the series, so disappointing. Although murder mystery and whodunit were still at the essence of the plotline, <i>Ghost Story</i> felt like a different kind of book, whether that’s for good or worse, it’s up to you to decide. After all the destruction that happened at the end of <i>Changes</i>, it’s not a surprise that the focus on this book is targeted towards Molly, Murphy, and the side characters more than Harry. I did enjoy reading Harry’s background with Justin DuMorne very much, but it was Harry’s feelings towards his companions and vice versa that really made the book for me.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “Doing nothing is difficult. Once you aren’t busy, your head starts chewing things over. Dark, bleak thoughts appear. You start to think about what your life means.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><i>Ghost Story</i> featured a lot of introspective moments, and I loved it. As I repeatedly said, more than the action scenes and practically everything else in the series, I love <i>The Dresden Files</i> for the characters and the continuous—though relatively slow—progress in their development. The action scenes in this book, unlike <i>Changes</i>, unfortunately, returned to that “too long for its own good” phase. The revelation behind the murder mystery was done well, in my opinion, but the actions that led up to it became quite boring quickly.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “Courage is about learning how to function despite the fear, to put aside your instincts to run or give in completely to the anger born from fear. Courage is about using your brain and your heart when every cell of your body is screaming at your to fight or flee - and then following through on what you believe is the right thing to do.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I highly enjoyed reading <i>Ghost Story</i>. Although the tone of the book was the bleakest so far, the narrative was filled with heartfelt, sad, and at the same time, hopeful moments to counter it. Feel free to ignore my criticisms of the longevity of the action scenes; it is a recurring issue for me with this series, and I have a good feeling I’m on a very unpopular opinion side on this notion. Argh, I can’t believe I only have three—soon to be four—published books in the series to read. I am both excited and sad. I will embrace <i>Cold Days</i> within the next two weeks!<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “Pain isn’t a lot of fun, at least not for most folks, but it is utterly unique to life. Pain — physical, emotional, and otherwise — is the shadow cast by everything you want out of life, the alternative to the result you were hoping for, and the inevitable creator of strength. From the pain of our failures we learn to be better, stronger, greater than what we were before. Pain is there to tell us when we’ve done something badly—it’s a teacher, a guide, one that is always there to both warn us of our limitations and challenge us to overcome them.<br><br>For something no one likes, pain does us a whole hell of a lot of good.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><b>Picture: <i>Ghost Story</i> by Vincent Chong</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1599904293i/30095926._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9780451464071/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u> | <u><a href="https://bookshop.org/a/1165/9780451464071" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookshop (Support Local Bookstores!) </a></u></b><br><br><b>You can find <u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2020/09/12/book-review-ghost-story-the-dresden-files-13-by-jim-butcher/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u> and the rest of my reviews at <u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b><br><br><i>Special thanks to my Patrons on <b><u><a href="https://www.patreon.com/petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Patreon</a></u></b> for giving me extra support towards my passion for reading and reviewing!<br><br>My Patrons: Alfred, Alya, Annabeth, Devin, Diana, Hamad, Jimmy Nutts, Joie, Michelle, Mike, Miracle, Nicholas, Zoe.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5220959220253252054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_107771635" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107771635" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107771635?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107771635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7724695172832103517">Six months after his death, Harry Dresden returns to Chicago to solve his own murder. Can he keep his friends safe in the process?<br/><br/>I've got a lot to say about this. I'll cover the good points first.<br/><br/><b>The Good:</b> Having a ghost come back to solve his own murder isn't a new idea but Butcher did a fairly good job with it here. The supporting cast, Molly in particular, developed quite a bit in Harry's absence. The new character of Fitz has potential, as does Mortimer, who I don't particularly remember. T</span>
  <span id="freeText7724695172832103517" style="display:none">Six months after his death, Harry Dresden returns to Chicago to solve his own murder. Can he keep his friends safe in the process?<br /><br />I've got a lot to say about this. I'll cover the good points first.<br /><br /><b>The Good:</b> Having a ghost come back to solve his own murder isn't a new idea but Butcher did a fairly good job with it here. The supporting cast, Molly in particular, developed quite a bit in Harry's absence. The new character of Fitz has potential, as does Mortimer, who I don't particularly remember. The intrigue with the faerie court is always a plus.<br /><br /><b>The Bad:</b> I just can't stand Harry Dresden any more. He's like that friend you thought was hilarious in the sixth grade but wanted to strangle by the time you got out of high school. He's an unfunny smart ass with a "funny" quip for every situation. Worse yet, 70% of the characters in the series talk just like him. His Star Wars references are really tired and he's had no significant character development since the series began.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />Another of the things that bothered be, and they are legion, is that Butcher can't seem to commit to anything that might move the series along. Remember that war between the White Council and their unseen enemy? Yeah, whatever happened with that? That subplot hasn't advanced AT ALL in the last two books. Robert Jordan's corpse called. He said you should pick up the pace and start wrapping this shit up while people still care about it.<br /><br />Remember how the entire Red Court was killed in the last book at Chichen Itza? Not 50 pages into this book, there was speculation that not all of them were killed. WTF, Butcher? How about growing a pair and sticking with your guns for once?<br /><br />Here's another thing that bugs me. Harry comes back from the dead at the end. He was already the biggest Gary Stu character around before he came back. Now that death apparently can't stop him, why should I give a shit about him anymore?<br /><br />Did anyone else notice how the women can't seem to get along without Harry Dresden for six months without falling apart but the men do just fine? Just pointing it out.<br /><br />The resolution to Harry's death? Whatever. It was just there for me and seemed a bit illogical considering he had a daughter to look after.<br /><br />I think my issues with the series stem from the fact that while it's an episodic detective series, Butcher's trying to instill it with an epic feel. The problem is that he can tell a detective story or one that advances the overall plot but can't seem to ever do both at the same time.<br /><br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>The Ugly:</b> There comes a time in many relationships to call it quits. Harry Dresden, for us, that day is today. There was a time when the release of a new Harry Dresden book excited me like a pedophile at a pre-teen beauty pageant. I'd snap up the newest book and go after it like Amy Winehouse and a vial of crack. But those days are long gone. I've been going through the motions for the last couple of books and it just isn't working for me anymore. I keep hoping things will get better but they don't. The tediousness continues and I'm ready to move on. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7724695172832103517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_123669357" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123669357" />
    <a title="Regina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3104032-regina"><img alt="Regina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362864551p2/3104032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123669357?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Regina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Regina" href="/user/show/3104032-regina">Regina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=owned-kindle">owned-kindle</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123669357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8521247568601588075">I love Harry. I love Bob. I love Molly. I love the new and improved Butters. I loved seeing Daniel Carpenter. I love this series. It just is such a comfort read for me. I had forgotten how much I love this series until I started to read this book. The mystery and quest were interesting and unlike much urban fantasy, it was unique – nothing I have read before. Maybe a little of Harry Potter, but I am okay with that. One of the things that is so fantastic about this series is that there are conseq</span>
  <span id="freeText8521247568601588075" style="display:none">I love Harry. I love Bob. I love Molly. I love the new and improved Butters. I loved seeing Daniel Carpenter. I love this series. It just is such a comfort read for me. I had forgotten how much I love this series until I started to read this book. The mystery and quest were interesting and unlike much urban fantasy, it was unique – nothing I have read before. Maybe a little of Harry Potter, but I am okay with that. One of the things that is so fantastic about this series is that there are consequences. Consequences to dying, consequences to losing loved ones, and consequences to killing. Harry is self reflective and looks back on his actions – he considers what he should have done and questions his own actions. He has regret. <br /><br />This is such a rich, beautiful story. Action – of course there is action, but now too much. Some of the Dresden books have too much action in my opinion, but this one has a great balance. Some of the characters reactions to situations frustrated me, but they were reacting in a very human way. I also enjoy how Butcher revisits past baddies. In most books, the baddies die and everything is solved and the heroes move on to their next quest. Not in this world. In this world, it isn’t that the baddies don’t die, but there are reverberations – so that past decisions to take out the bad guys or remove them have caused new problems to arise. <br /><br />Butcher has gotten better at describing Chicago, but I still saw some factual inaccuracies that drive my crazy. For example, when he was examining a priest’s night table he notes that one of the only earthly goods the priest owns is a King James bible, but Catholics don’t read the King James bible and in fact the Catholic bible is slightly different than the protestant bible. Minor, but I am shocked an editor or Butcher didn’t catch this. I just like being immersed in a story but when there is a glaring factual error, it takes me out of the story. However, I loved this story so much I am still giving it 5 stars. <br /><br /><br /><br />*****<br /><b>More New Updates:!!!! woohooo!!!!!!</b><br /><br />Our GHOST STORY preview continues with Chapter 3!<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jim-butcher.com/books/dresden/ghost-story/ghost-story-chapter-3">http://www.jim-butcher.com/books/dres...</a><br /><br />If you missed last week's post, you can check them out here: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jim-butcher.com/books/dresden/ghost-story/ghost-story-chapter-1">http://www.jim-butcher.com/books/dres...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jim-butcher.com/books/dresden/ghost-story/ghost-story-chapter-2">http://www.jim-butcher.com/books/dres...</a><br /><br />We'll be posting 5 chapters in all over the coming weeks, plus video of Jim reading chapters 1-4 at the NYCC Fan Dinner last October!<br /><br />**<br />With a little over a month remaining until GHOST STORY's release, it's time for some sample chapters! <br /><br />Chapter 1: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jim-butcher.com/books/dresden/ghost-story/ghost-story-chapter-1">http://www.jim-butcher.com/books/dres...</a><br />Chapter 2: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jim-butcher.com/books/dresden/ghost-story/ghost-story-chapter-2">http://www.jim-butcher.com/books/dres...</a><br /><br />In all, we’ll be posting five sample chapters, plus bonus audio of Jim reading the first four chapters at the NY Comic Con Fan Dinner! (NOTE: You should definitely read the text version before listening to Jim read. He was reading from an earlier draft, and some aspects have changed slightly.) They will be posted on the following schedule:<br /><br />June 28th: Chapter 3<br />July 5th: Chapter 4, plus the audio for 1 and 2.<br />July 12th: Chapter 5, plus the audio for 3 and 4.<br />July 26th: Release day!<br /><br />You can pre-order GHOST STORY from our store or through the Virtual Signing, which now also includes the DFRPG!<br />Our Store: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jim-butcher.com/store">http://www.jim-butcher.com/store</a><br />The Virtual Signing: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jim-butcher.com/posts/2011/virtual-signing-for-ghost-story-and-side-jobs">http://www.jim-butcher.com/posts/2011...</a><br /><br />Also, don't forget that the Virtual Signing for Codex Alera map posters ends on June 28th, just over a week away! If you want a map signed by Jim and Priscilla, the artist, get your pre-order in soon.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://priscellie.com/store/">http://priscellie.com/store/</a><br /><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.penguingroup.com/static/pages/extras/ghoststory/index.html">http://us.penguingroup.com/static/pag...</a><br /><br />You can also download GHOST STORY desktop wallpaper here:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jim-butcher.com/posts/2011/changes-paperback">http://www.jim-butcher.com/posts/2011...</a><br /><br />In the month leading up to the July 26th release, we'll have even more GHOST STORY goodies for you, here at Jim-Butcher.com. <span id="freeTextContainer9928068723829273031"> This was a very uneven book, with lots of filler material. Harry lives to fight again. It's as if he never left. It's as if we're back to square one. Shoot, Jim Butcher has officially exhausted any permutations of wisdom that used to guarantee 5 stars from me. This book... such a bland book with a sugary end tacked on. One piece of advice to demanding readers; you'll enjoy the rest of this series only if you lower your expectations as much as you can.</span>

<div id="review_3193745598" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3193745598" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3193745598?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3193745598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4585497808152392831">Even though writing is a singular task, with an author slaving away (bleeding if we listen to Hemingway) in front of a keyboard, it is also very much a collaboration – besides assistants, the writer may likely gain insight and critical input from editors, publishers, agents, fans, friends, and family. Besides his or her own personal muse there is also the influence of peers, critics and the audience. There is also the nebulous and sundry inspirations from literature, art and pop culture.<br/><br/>Somewher</span>
  <span id="freeText4585497808152392831" style="display:none">Even though writing is a singular task, with an author slaving away (bleeding if we listen to Hemingway) in front of a keyboard, it is also very much a collaboration – besides assistants, the writer may likely gain insight and critical input from editors, publishers, agents, fans, friends, and family. Besides his or her own personal muse there is also the influence of peers, critics and the audience. There is also the nebulous and sundry inspirations from literature, art and pop culture.<br><br>Somewhere between the publication of the eleventh book on the Dresden Files, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3475161.Turn_Coat__The_Dresden_Files___11_" title="Turn Coat (The Dresden Files, #11) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Turn Coat</a> in 2009 and Butcher’s twelfth book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6585201.Changes__The_Dresden_Files___12_" title="Changes (The Dresden Files, #12) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Changes</a>, in 2010, there must have been a very important, persuasive, series changing discussion or dialogue. What had been a fun but somewhat formulaic series up to Turn Coat became a thought provoking and bold, genre defining series in Changes and those paradigm shifts continue in spades in Butcher’s LUCKY thirteen novel in the Dresden Files – Ghost Story.<br><br>There is such a distinction between this work and those that precede it, a reviewer will have a difficult time appraising without laying down mines of spoilers for unwary but interested readers.<br><br>Let’s just say that Harry’s perspective is wildly altered and he’s operating with radically different magic rules.<br><br>I had, after reading Changes, opined that it was the best Dresden novel to date. And I stand by that declaration, until you read Ghost Story, which I now see as the best.<br><br>Butcher has Harry confront a panoply of complications largely without the aid of his magic. Dresden is a man of action and has frequently been able to fix problems with the brute force of his will and spells. In Ghost Story we see Harry operating from the shadows, very much out of his element and Butcher rises to the narrative challenge by laying down a tight, well written paranormal thriller.<br><br>Dresden fans will get lots of action and will see many of the recurring characters of the series. Most noteworthy is Butcher’s dynamic portrayal of Molly Carpenter and a fresh look at Butters and Morty Lindquist.<br><br>So good I want to watch old Patrick Swayze films and start the next one.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1582308416i/29000664.jpg" width="250" height="297" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="4585497808152392831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134023016" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134023016?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=action">action</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134023016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8039650925945735059">Okay...so I'm a Dresden junkie. I got the book yesterday and finished it (this time LOL) at 1:30 this morning.<br/><br/>The book picks up pretty much as the last book ends and.....****************** NOTE: THIS REVIEW WILL CONTAIN SPOILERS FOR THE LAST BOOK, CHANGES. I WILL BE ASSUMING THAT IF YOU ARE READING GHOST STORY YOU HAVE READ CHANGES...........<br/><br/><br/><br/>Okay, as I was saying, the book picks up pretty much as the last book (Changes) ends, though time doesn't run in death as it does here.<br/><br/>Don't ask me, I don't</span>
  <span id="freeText8039650925945735059" style="display:none">Okay...so I'm a Dresden junkie. I got the book yesterday and finished it (this time LOL) at 1:30 this morning.<br /><br />The book picks up pretty much as the last book ends and.....****************** NOTE: THIS REVIEW WILL CONTAIN SPOILERS FOR THE LAST BOOK, CHANGES. I WILL BE ASSUMING THAT IF YOU ARE READING GHOST STORY YOU HAVE READ CHANGES...........<br /><br /><br /><br />Okay, as I was saying, the book picks up pretty much as the last book (Changes) ends, though time doesn't run in death as it does here.<br /><br />Don't ask me, I don't know why.<br /><br />Harry having died is probably a little relieved that he might get to lay back and "rest in peace" (though his ultimate after-life disposition does concern him a bit). He's still a little preoccupied about leading everyone who cares/cared about him on what seemed pretty much a suicide mission...oh and murdering his child's mother. But hey everyone has a bad day now and then right?<br /><br />Unfortunately upon arriving at "Between" (that's apparently "between life and death" though Harry never really gets a straight answer to that either.), Harry finds that he's not moving on to anything as simple and restful as hell, no there were..."irregularities" about his death.<br /><br />So what else is new for Harry? Should he (or for that matter we) have been surprised or expected anything else? <br /><br />Anyone who's read many of my posts knows that I am a Jim Butcher fan. And while there could be said to be some "issues" with the books it says something that none of them are "deal-breakers" for me. (For example, don't get your theology from novels...) I have read all these books (and most of the Codex Alera books, a few of those still to go). I snap up the Dresden books as soon as I can, and I recommend them. There will always be a matter of taste with any book or series of books. I enjoy Mr. Butcher's turn of phrase, I enjoy his sense of humor and I enjoy his story telling. This book has all those things and moves our main character into a situation (or set of situations) that is (are) not typical of what we've seen before.<br /><br />What's good and what's not so good here? Well, on the "not so good" side there may be a bit of a feeling that things are moving a bit slowly. By that I don't mean there's a lack of action, anything but. I mean that for those of us who see the Story moving or trying to move forward there may be times that it starts to feel that we're sort of taking a couple of steps back before we move forward. (And I'm not really talking about the flashback sequences there.)Personally I thought Harry himself moved forward a bit slowly here. There were for me a few times I felt a little like I was circling, but be aware, it didn't really gripe me. The story flowed and the gaps were/are getting filled in. There is obviously a saga building. As one character says (I won't say who as that might be spoilerish) "it's one of those "it's about the journey not the destination" things".<br /><br />You are going to find out a bit more about Harry's background here, get a look at a couple of things we've only seen mentioned in passing before and also begin considering things from a totally different perspective. <br /><br />So...good book. Highly recommended, as a matter of fact, my highest "brain candy" recommendation.I'll list it among my favorites along with the rest of the series. I'm now awaiting the announcement of the release date for Cold Days. Pathetic huh? LOL <br /><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I had "indulged" in much discussion as to who was behind Harry's murder. A friend here on Goodreads had suggested that Harry himself might have been behind it. I had dismissed this because Harry had given the "big promise" to Mab that he wouldn't suicide. The idea that he would ask Molly to "mess in his head" thus breaking the laws of magic (and worse asking Molly to break the laws of magic) also further damaging Molly was something I didn't think Harry would do... I was of course, wrong. <br /><br />I assume this is/was all part of the Harry has gone too far; Harry has crossed a line point. Uriel opens a lot up for Harry when he lets Harry look at what he (Harry)said and did. When Harry said he'd let the world burn to save Maggie he was (in effect) saying he'd let Molly burn (and of course by extension Thomas, Butters, Mouse and Mister...and Murphy burn). Not to mention he had to realize that he was saying to save his daughter he would kill or allow to die a lot of other father's daughters.<br /><br />A lot still coming...how will he interact with Mab, what happened with Bob... Who or what is the parasite... who whispered in his ear... ?<br /><br />Hope I live to see the series complete. Come on Jim, I'm closing on 60. LOL  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8039650925945735059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2608677320" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2608677320" />
    <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader"><img alt="Heidi The Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593309467p2/7986781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2608677320?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fantasy-and-sci-fi">fantasy-and-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2608677320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10214774323173923494">Harry Dresden, wizard for hire, is dead. And he still has to save the world by discovering his killer. How is that fair?<br/><br/><i>Maybe I was dead, but I was sure as hell not ready to go. I had to make sure the people who'd helped me take on the Red King were taken care of.</i> pgs 32-33<br/><br/>He quickly discovers that magic and dead people don't mix. Now, instead of taking on god-like enemies with the backing of the Winter Queen, he can't even pass through thresholds without permission.<br/><br/>It's frustrating for both Har</span>
  <span id="freeText10214774323173923494" style="display:none">Harry Dresden, wizard for hire, is dead. And he still has to save the world by discovering his killer. How is that fair?<br /><br /><i>Maybe I was dead, but I was sure as hell not ready to go. I had to make sure the people who'd helped me take on the Red King were taken care of.</i> pgs 32-33<br /><br />He quickly discovers that magic and dead people don't mix. Now, instead of taking on god-like enemies with the backing of the Winter Queen, he can't even pass through thresholds without permission.<br /><br />It's frustrating for both Harry and the reader. I didn't realize how much I enjoyed reading about Harry blowing stuff up until he couldn't do it anymore.<br /><br /><i>One of the things a lot of people don't understand about magic is that the rules of how it works aren't hard-and-fast; they're fluid, changing with time, with the seasons, with location, and with the intent of a practitioner.</i> pg 179. And if you're alive or dead.<br /><br />We spend a lot of time in Harry's mind and memory in <i>Ghost Story</i> and less time in action. Frankly, it's not as much fun as the other books in the series.<br /><br /><i>"You have entered a new world. Your old life is no more. You cannot be a part of it any longer. The wide universe stretches before you."</i> pg 185<br /><br />I also didn't realize how much I enjoyed the give-and-take of the characters in this series until the main character couldn't interact with most of them anymore.<br /><br /><i>Ghosts who weren't supermighty manifested all the time. It wasn't a question of raw power, and it never had been — it was a matter of desire. You just had to be crazy enough to make it happen."</i> pg 550<br /><br />That being said, the ending of this book was strangely satisfying. And I cried at the part with Mouse. Overall, I'm glad I read it, but I'm not of the opinion that it was the best in the series.<br /><br />I would have already started on the next book but there's a wait list for the digital copy. Library user problems, sigh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10214774323173923494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13891422542802586688">Holey Moley! At the end of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6585201.Changes__The_Dresden_Files___12_' title='Changes (The Dresden Files, #12) by Jim Butcher' rel='nofollow noopener'>Changes</a> when wizard Harry Dresden is shot, I thought No, Harry can't be dead - surely Jim Butcher will find some clever way to bring him back to life. But I was very wrong, Harry is dead and in this book his ghost is sent back to Chicago to prevent the death of three of his closest friends and to find out who killed him.<br/><br/>The Chicago Harry is sent back to is a very different one to the one he left six months before. The vacuum he created by destroying the Red Court of va</span>
  <span id="freeText13891422542802586688" style="display:none">Holey Moley! At the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6585201.Changes__The_Dresden_Files___12_" title="Changes (The Dresden Files, #12) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Changes</a> when wizard Harry Dresden is shot, I thought No, Harry can't be dead - surely Jim Butcher will find some clever way to bring him back to life. But I was very wrong, Harry is dead and in this book his ghost is sent back to Chicago to prevent the death of three of his closest friends and to find out who killed him.<br /><br />The Chicago Harry is sent back to is a very different one to the one he left six months before. The vacuum he created by destroying the Red Court of vampires has been filled by malicious paranormal entities and the city has become a battleground. His friend Murphy and apprentice Molly are both riddled with guild over his death and not in a good place. As a ghost Harry has none of the powers he had in life as a wizard and has to learn how to use his spirit form to communicate with his mortal friends and to prevent being devoured by other spirits. Harry being Harry comes up with various inventive ways of helping his friends in their fight against the forces trying to control their world.<br /><br />This book feels like a bridge to whatever is to come next in the series. There is less action and more introspection and reminiscing on Harry's part than in previous episodes where the action was pretty much non stop. I think in some ways that was to give Harry a sense of closure of the important things in his previous life as the end of the book suggests that the next chapter in Harry's story will be very different - but hopefully no less exciting.</span>

<div id="review_460617578" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/460617578" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/460617578?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460617578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6100844259759704629">I can only give 2.5 stars plus 0.5 out of my respect for the series. Harry was sent back to the world of mortals as a ghost to investigate his own murder. When he came back, Chicago changed a lot - and not for the good. Yet another new enemies appeared, worse than the old ones - as usual. Oh yeah, we never actually see them. Harry's friends changed, too.<br/><br/>There are several problems with the book. <br/><br/>Harry is first and foremost an action hero constantly on his guilt trip, but when this trip happens to</span>
  <span id="freeText6100844259759704629" style="display:none">I can only give 2.5 stars plus 0.5 out of my respect for the series. Harry was sent back to the world of mortals as a ghost to investigate his own murder. When he came back, Chicago changed a lot - and not for the good. Yet another new enemies appeared, worse than the old ones - as usual. Oh yeah, we never actually see them. Harry's friends changed, too.<br /><br />There are several problems with the book. <br /><br />Harry is first and foremost an action hero constantly on his guilt trip, but when this trip happens to be between the action bits, it is not too bad. This time he cannot do anything to material things, so what he does the whole book is talking a lot and feeling guilty for anything and everything (I was seriously expecting him to find a way to blame himself for Crucifixion of Jesus; I kid you not, I would not be surprise if he did). <br /><br />The repeating parts of the series finally beginning to get old for me. After reading description of Soulgaze for thirteenth time I can repeat it in my sleep. I am ashamed to say, I was glad Harry's apartment was destroyed in the previous book as I hoped I will not have to read its description yet again. Boy was I wrong! Luckily where was nothing about his car in this book, which is a blessing, I guess. <br /><br />I really did not like the way the characters of Butters and Murphy is developing. Butters was great because he was never an action hero, just a guy with (barely) enough courage to do the right thing. In this book, he is doing an action hero thing. Murphy does not want to look into Harry's murder because she is afraid that she would find a proof of guilt of her boyfriend (?). Is this the way a really strong woman should behave? <br /><br />Is it too much to ask that villains killed by Dresden stay dead? For now only good guys stay dead, almost every bad person/entity comes back one way or the other.<br /><br />I might have read too many books of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Agatha Christie</a>, but I figured Harry's murder sometime in the first half of the book, so no big surprises in this case.<br /><br />All in all, I consider this to be just a filling material and hope the next book is better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6100844259759704629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_190621337" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190621337" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/163750-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1189653481p2/163750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190621337?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/163750-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=mystery-contemp-american">mystery-contemp-american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=read-more-than-once">read-more-than-once</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=fierce-females">fierce-females</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=werecreatures">werecreatures</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer190621337&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190621337" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17872596791515401966">First read: 26-30 July, 2011.<br/>Re-read: November, 2012<br/><br/>Obviously, someone who's read this far in the series is a fan. For anyone unfamiliar with Dresden, this is not the book to start with. There are lots of fascinating, cool, poignant, and funny things about this book I could go on and on about, but if you've read the book, you already know about them. I've put a spoiler-cloak on this because of the one major plot point I am going to mention, just in case someone who isn't up to speed yet is surfi</span>
  <span id="freeText17872596791515401966" style="display:none">First read: 26-30 July, 2011.<br />Re-read: November, 2012<br /><br />Obviously, someone who's read this far in the series is a fan. For anyone unfamiliar with Dresden, this is not the book to start with. There are lots of fascinating, cool, poignant, and funny things about this book I could go on and on about, but if you've read the book, you already know about them. I've put a spoiler-cloak on this because of the one major plot point I am going to mention, just in case someone who isn't up to speed yet is surfing reviews. <br />Butcher didn't disappoint me. While the "mostly dead" plot can drive me crazy at times, it's crafted well here. I kept turning the pages, eager to see how it would all turn out and sometimes wondering if Butcher really was going to sucker punch us, after all. As I (and, no doubt, tons of other fans) always suspected, Butcher could not let the plotline of Harry becoming Winter Knight go to waste. I figured either Lea or Mab would save Harry, and it turned out to be Mab. The <i>why</i> of Harry's shooting, however, turned out to be much more amazing than the <i>who</i> or the <i>how</i>. <br />It was great to see so many recurring characters again, interacting in new ways. In particular, Molly, Murphy, and Butters had me both impressed and worried. <br />Butcher has such a way with the narrative voice. After 13 novels, 1 book of short stories, and a graphic novel, it's almost as if Harry is someone I know, talking to me. He is one of my all-time favourite fictional characters now--flawed, noble, sweet, goofy, damaged, angry, funny, clever, complex. I really enjoyed the backstory in this one, about Harry's childhood and teenage years. All the humour and pop culture references are so much fun for us SFF geeks, too, on top of Butcher's clever use of various aspects of legend and myth. <br />The Dresdenverse has become a much different place since the events of <i>Changes</i>, and there is a lot of potential for fascinating new plots. I look forward to continuing the journey. <br />I'm also going to re-read <i>Changes</i> and <i>Ghost Story</i> back-to-back to look closely at how they fit together before the release of the next book.<br /><br />On the second reading (6-21 November, 2012), I do think <i>Changes</i> and <i>Ghost Story</i> flow together well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17872596791515401966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer387421422767978395"><b> <i> ***Please note that this review will contain spoilers from the last book in the series.*** </i><br/><br/>To save his friends—and his own soul—Harry will have to pull off the ultimate trick without any magic... </b><br/><br/>This one was so good! Ghost Story starts right where Changes left off with Harry roaming around in a place that is between life and death, where he observes his friends and promptly becomes worried for them. The main thing I wanted from this book was to find out who shot Harry in the last one, and of </span>
  <span id="freeText387421422767978395" style="display:none"><b> <i> ***Please note that this review will contain spoilers from the last book in the series.*** </i><br /><br />To save his friends—and his own soul—Harry will have to pull off the ultimate trick without any magic... </b><br /><br />This one was so good! Ghost Story starts right where Changes left off with Harry roaming around in a place that is between life and death, where he observes his friends and promptly becomes worried for them. The main thing I wanted from this book was to find out who shot Harry in the last one, and of course I also wanted to find out how he was going to be brought back to life, because we all know this isn't the last book in the series, and we can't have The Dresden Files series without Harry. Let's just say I didn't see that explanation coming. <br /><br />In the last book Harry did a few things that surprised me all on behalf of his daughter and he continued to surprise me in this book as well. Ghost Story in general was a little different from the rest of the series, but I liked it, it really moved me. As always I'm looking forward to the next book in the series.<br /><br />Review also posted at <a href="https://writingsofareader.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Writings of a Reader</a><br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1260651476" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1260651476" />
    <a title="Tracey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/841949-tracey"><img alt="Tracey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325394892p2/841949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1260651476?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracey" href="/user/show/841949-tracey">Tracey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780147520456" href="/book/show/25065650-ghost-story">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/841949-tracey?shelf=chicago">chicago</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/841949-tracey?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/841949-tracey?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/841949-tracey?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/841949-tracey?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1260651476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5043286156588297870">Well, bless Audible's little heart. One spring morning I received this email: <br/><br/>"Dear Listener,<br/><br/>Here at Audible, we truly understand the power great performances bring to your favorite stories. And for long-running series, no matter how good a new voice may be, it can be hard to hear someone else bring beloved characters to life. So when Ghost Story: A Novel of the Dresden Files, Book 13, was narrated by someone other than series regular James Marsters, some listeners were disappointed. <br/><br/>We're happy</span>
  <span id="freeText5043286156588297870" style="display:none">Well, bless Audible's little heart. One spring morning I received this email: <br /><br />"Dear Listener,<br /><br />Here at Audible, we truly understand the power great performances bring to your favorite stories. And for long-running series, no matter how good a new voice may be, it can be hard to hear someone else bring beloved characters to life. So when Ghost Story: A Novel of the Dresden Files, Book 13, was narrated by someone other than series regular James Marsters, some listeners were disappointed. <br /><br />We're happy to report that Ghost Story has since been re-recorded with the inimitable Marsters at the helm - and, since you're a fan of this series, we want you to have it free."<br /><br />"Disappointed" didn't quite cover it. <br /><br />I want to create a movie–style poster for this book, with a one–word tagline: "BOO".<br /> <br /><i>Ghost Story</i> is one of those books whose end – even if you kind of pretty much know it's coming – was still enough to rock me back on my heels. And to make me want to go back and listen to the book again, to pay attention to all those things that didn't seem to need so much attention the first time around.<br /> <br />This interlude teaches Harry some valuable lessons – unable to act, he learns to consider more than he's ever had the chance to do before. A valuable trait, considering what is to come.<br /> <br />See, this is why I tend not to write reviews of these series that I love so much. For one thing, I started reading Dresden back <s>in the Cretaceous</s> not too long after it was published, before I was really in the habit of writing reviews at all. Fast forward fifteen years (!), and I've read the first books a few times each, and Harry's in my bloodstream. Harry and Molly and Mouse and Mister and old Uncle Tom Cobley and all are part of my life. While the books are (or at least can be) very different from each other, it's hard to keep all my reviews from coming out very much the same: "I love Harry Dresden, I adore James Marsters, I am in love with James Marsters reading Harry Dresden, these books are great", etc. I should look on it as an exercise in writing: how to write the same love song over and over, some fifteen times by now, and make it readable… but I don't. <br /> <br />Ghost Story, of course, is not your usual Harry Dresden insofar as there is a usual Harry Dresden, and so …<br /> <br />One review I saw mentions that the reviewer is tired of Harry Dresden, doesn't find him funny anymore. <br /><br />I do. I'm not. Maybe it's partly James Marsters reading it; maybe it's not. I don't know. I don't care. I'm still having a great time after fifteen books (and this, #13, twice in seven months), and I would be very happy indeed to know that Harry and Jim Butcher and I will all get very very old together. <br /> <br /><i>And then there was the famous flying broomstick incident of Wacker Drive…</i><br /> <br />Surprisingly, I think I laughed <i>more</i> listening to this audiobook than the others in the series. If there was any doubt that Harry Dresden and Jim Butcher are big ol' geek–nerds, this puts paid to that idea. Harry's new "superpowers" ("BAMF!" made me so very happy), and the quote he uses to prove he is himself, and the Gandalf internal monologue, and so on – so wonderful.<br /> <br />And: <i>I mean, go figure. You prepare your home for an assault and you don't take zombies into consideration. I'd fallen victim to one of the other classic blunders, along with not getting involved in a land war in Asia and never going in against a Sicilian when death was on the line.</i><br /> <br />AND a Pink Floyd reference: "How can you have any pudding if you don't eat your meat?" Well done, sir.<br /> <br />"There are two kinds of people in the world, Molly: Star Wars fans, and Star Trek fans. This is shocking." Look, Mister Wizard, you can identify who's what on the Old Trek bridge, so just you shush.<br /> <br />(I still wonder why Harry never saw Firefly, though. Maybe because it didn't last long enough on tv and his VCR/DVD player tends to malfunction – ?)<br /> <br />But there was also, kind of obviously, a lot of heart–string–yanking (nothing so gentle as tugging here). There is a really lovely story about that time Justin DuMorne gave Harry a baseball glove … and then a few minutes later he relates the fact that Justin trained him how to shield himself by throwing fastballs at him. Damn. As if I needed another reason for my heart to bleed for the very young Harry.<br /> <br /> I should, I suppose, take a step back and acknowledge that, much as I do love Marsters, these aren't perfect narrations. Take, for example, the phrase "sleeping quarters"; emphasis on the wrong word changes the meaning rather a bit. That sort of thing happens now and then, as with most narrators. But then I need to take that step forward again and reiterate that I really don't care. It's not perfect; it <i>is</i> more enjoyable than I would ever dare to expect.<br /> <br />Harry says, <i>Girls don't flock to the guy who drives the old car, reads a lot of books, and kicks down the doors of living nightmares. </i><br /> <br />Harry, you've been hanging out with the wrong women.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5043286156588297870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/633431414?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mr. Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mr. Matt" href="/user/show/15984059-mr-matt">Mr. Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15984059-mr-matt?shelf=fantasy-urban">fantasy-urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15984059-mr-matt?shelf=2013">2013</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer633431414" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11553852003737201594">I struggled to rate this book, finally deciding on 3 out of 5 stars. <br/><br/>I gave it three stars mainly because Ghost Story does what the other books do well. I like reading about Harry's world and the characters in it. Jim Butcher has really brought them to life in a plausible, believable world. Moreover, the action is good, and there is always a unique twist. I also liked the way Mort's character developed into a really sympathetic good guy. I also liked Molly's changes. <br/><br/>Unfortunately, I think my en</span>
  <span id="freeText11553852003737201594" style="display:none">I struggled to rate this book, finally deciding on 3 out of 5 stars. <br /><br />I gave it three stars mainly because Ghost Story does what the other books do well. I like reading about Harry's world and the characters in it. Jim Butcher has really brought them to life in a plausible, believable world. Moreover, the action is good, and there is always a unique twist. I also liked the way Mort's character developed into a really sympathetic good guy. I also liked Molly's changes. <br /><br />Unfortunately, I think my enchantment with Harry Dresden may be coming to a close. This book seemed to manifest almost everything that I've really started to dislike about the series. The author seems determined to make Harry "The One" and in this book, wow. Harry dies, fights the bad guys as a ghost, and ends up returning to life. Jeez! (Pun intended). Divine intervention by one of the main archangels is required to move the story. I was struggling to buy the line the author was selling. Outside of that, what ever happened to the Fommor? Maybe I missed it, but wasn't there a group of modified humans led by a mysterious supernatural community that was moving in on the Red Court's former territory? The Corpsetaker was allied with them. Harry &amp; company dealt with the Corpsetaker (thanks to Mort and Molly!) but whatever happened to the Fommor? (To be fair, I may have missed it as I struggled at points in the book).<br /><br />Long story short, if you like Harry, you'll probably be okay with the book. If not, it might be too much. Just my two cents.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14900573126801270010">Harry Dresden for President! (This week anyway!) I really enjoyed this story. It was pretty interesting watching Harry in ghost form trying to save his friends without a body!<br/>I love Dresden's character. He is prepared to throw down against an angel when he thought she was going to take one of his friends, he defends the weak and powerless, and will do anything for those he loves and for the majority of the time it is this character trait that gets him into so much trouble. He has always been a s</span>
  <span id="freeText14900573126801270010" style="display:none">Harry Dresden for President! (This week anyway!) I really enjoyed this story. It was pretty interesting watching Harry in ghost form trying to save his friends without a body!<br />I love Dresden's character. He is prepared to throw down against an angel when he thought she was going to take one of his friends, he defends the weak and powerless, and will do anything for those he loves and for the majority of the time it is this character trait that gets him into so much trouble. He has always been a strong believer in doing the right thing and managed to avoid crossing the moral line until the previous book.<br />The pay off comes in these books now as we have a long history of getting to know Dresden's friends, who are as quirky and diverse as Dresden himself.<br />The highlight of this book for me was looking into the inside of Bob's skull- home! Recommended for all Dresden fans. Read the previous twelve first though!<br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/176133174?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=supernatural-mystery">supernatural-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=male-lead">male-lead</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer176133174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1263135099787761288">I enjoyed Ghost Story and found it to be a decent progression in the series. Butcher continues to improve and Dresden continues to evolve. The idea of being a ghost was genius; it's interesting to see Dresden powerless, and forced to use other skills. It switches up the dynamic of the normal conflict in the series. I especially appreciated Harry taking responsibility for his decisions to involve Molly in his fanatical fight against the Red Court. Still too many red herrings, but it's a relief to</span>
  <span id="freeText1263135099787761288" style="display:none">I enjoyed Ghost Story and found it to be a decent progression in the series. Butcher continues to improve and Dresden continues to evolve. The idea of being a ghost was genius; it's interesting to see Dresden powerless, and forced to use other skills. It switches up the dynamic of the normal conflict in the series. I especially appreciated Harry taking responsibility for his decisions to involve Molly in his fanatical fight against the Red Court. Still too many red herrings, but it's a relief to have a few major points resolved.<br /><br />I'm sure I have more for a review, but just don't feel I can give it justice at the moment. Quite honestly, Butcher and his alter-ego Dresden irritate me part of the time and I can't put my finger on why.</span>

<div id="review_192722749" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192722749" />
    <a title="Fonzie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5103273-fonzie"><img alt="Fonzie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192722749?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fonzie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fonzie" href="/user/show/5103273-fonzie">Fonzie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192722749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12018789557858268616">Wow.<br/><br/>After the 4 plus months Butcher needed to write this I expected something epic. So I was a little fearful of finally reading the book - I mean I usually read them in one night and then have to wait a whole year for the next one.<br/><br/>Not this one, though. This book is a huge disappointment. I have been trying to read it for 3 days now, and couldn't get further than half of it. I keep drifting off to wash the dishes, collect laundry, read a better book even.<br/><br/>Gone is the wit, the sarcasm, the spark, </span>
  <span id="freeText12018789557858268616" style="display:none">Wow.<br /><br />After the 4 plus months Butcher needed to write this I expected something epic. So I was a little fearful of finally reading the book - I mean I usually read them in one night and then have to wait a whole year for the next one.<br /><br />Not this one, though. This book is a huge disappointment. I have been trying to read it for 3 days now, and couldn't get further than half of it. I keep drifting off to wash the dishes, collect laundry, read a better book even.<br /><br />Gone is the wit, the sarcasm, the spark, everything I loved in the previous books. This one is gritty and boring and moves at a snail's pace. It feels like Butcher had to fill more pages so he wrote fillers. Fluff. Oh and Sir Whatshisname is the most boring character in the series.<br /><br />This is not the real stuff. After 12 books of the Dresden files I stand bewildered, not sure if Butcher lost his touch or simply doesn't care. Maybe he expects us, that after 12 great books, we will lap it up no matter how bad it is? After pushing the release date back 4 months?! (Come to think of it, it should have been my first clue.)<br /><br />I'm disappointed. I can't stress how much.<br /><br />This book isn't worth it. And definitely wasn't worth the wait.<br /><br />*update*<br /><br />I finally finished it a few days ago.<br />The last third of the book did shed some light on what happened, why it happened. For me it wasn't much of a surprise to learn who killed Harry - or why. Sure, the "how" of it did interest me, and it was written nicely, but it still didn't make up for the utter boredom of the first half of the book.<br /><br />And even if the ending isn't as big of a cliffhanger as the last one, it still is one. I would be really annoyed if I liked the book and wanted more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12018789557858268616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17329672348457811178" style="display:none">I do love Harry Dresden, don't get me wrong, but he's a ghost solving his own murder in this book? Seriously? I'm supposed to take this seriously?<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/really" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

Like, been done - too many times - and not well - lame.<br><br>And, that's not the only problem I had with this particular book in the series. It was also incredibly boring. Harry was introspective. <i>Introspective!!!</i> That's just not Harry. He's a goofball. A wise-cracking, act-first think-later kind of guy. That's his charm. I mean, I get why. He had to see the fall-out from his decisions of the last book, but it was boring to read. Plus, it didn't actually change anything. He ended up where he started. Plus, after all of that introspection, he never actually truly understood why what he did to Molly was so very wrong. He still didn't quite get it. <br><br>The only two bright spots while trudging through this book were Bob &amp; Butter's relationship - which was awesome and fun, and Molly's transformation - which was scary.<br><br>I can't wait to get to the next book where Harry is back to himself again.
